## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This is a nonlinear harmonic oscillator where acceleration depends on position, velocity, and possibly time. The nonlinearity can arise from anharmonic restoring forces, nonlinear damping, or time-dependent driving, corresponding to well-known oscillator models like Duffing, van der Pol, or driven oscillators.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator (unforced): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * x**2 * v (nonlinear damping)
- Driven harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (periodic forcing)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (full Duffing)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order anharmonicity)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * x**2) (amplitude-dependent stiffness)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) (time-varying stiffness)
- Nonlinear damping with cubic velocity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity damping)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (velocity-dependent nonlinear friction)
- Combined van der Pol-Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * x**2 * v (combined nonlinearities)
- Coulomb + viscous damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sign(v) (mixed damping models)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) preserve symmetry of oscillation about equilibrium → use odd polynomial in x
- Nonlinear damping that allows self-sustained oscillations → terms like x²*v or (1-x²)*v (van der Pol type)
- Amplitude-dependent frequency shift → cubic or higher odd-power position terms (Duffing-type hardening/softening)
- Periodic external driving appears as sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) terms additive to the restoring/damping forces
- Energy-conserving systems have acceleration purely as a function of x (no v or t dependence) → gradient of potential
- Parametric resonance manifests as multiplicative coupling between x and trigonometric functions of t
- Limit cycle behavior requires at least one term where damping changes sign depending on amplitude → x²*v or v³ terms
- Phase-space symmetry: if the system is autonomous (no explicit t), acceleration depends only on x and v
